# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Kubernetes Controller Manager Work Queue and Rate Limiting

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in kubernetes/kubernetes that implement the controller work queue with rate limiting: the RateLimitingInterface, the ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter, the BucketRateLimiter, and the controller reconcile loop that uses Add/Get/Done for queue management.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the platform domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kubernetes--v1.32.0, sg-evals/client-go--v0.32.0, sg-evals/api--v0.32.0, sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/etcd-io-etcd` (etcd-io/etcd)

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive search and analysis of the Kubernetes controller work queue with rate limiting implementation. Here's what I found:

## Summary

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with detailed findings about the work queue and rate limiting system in kubernetes/kubernetes v1.32.0.

### Key Findings:

**Core Workqueue Architecture (4-layer design):**
1. **TypedInterface** (queue.go) - Basic FIFO queue with Add/Get/Done operations
2. **TypedDelayingInterface** (delaying_queue.go) - Adds AddAfter() for delayed requeuing
3. **TypedRateLimitingInterface** (rate_limiting_queue.go) - Adds AddRateLimited() with pluggable rate limiting
4. **Rate Limiter Strategies** (default_rate_limiters.go) - Multiple implementations

**Rate Limiting Implementations:**
- **TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter** - Exponential backoff per item (baseDelay * 2^failures)
- **TypedBucketRateLimiter** - Token bucket rate limiting (10 qps, 100 burst default)
- **TypedMaxOfRateLimiter** - Composes multiple limiters, returns worst-case delay
- **TypedItemFastSlowRateLimiter** - Fast retries then slow retries

**Controller Reconcile Loop Pattern:**
```
Run() → runWorker() → processNextWorkItem() {
  item, shutdown := queue.Get()
  defer queue.Done(item)
  
  err := syncHandler(item)
  if err != nil {
    queue.AddRateLimited(item)  // Auto rate-limited retry
  } else {
    queue.Forget(item)  // Clear retry state
  }
}
```

**20 Key Files** across the codebase including:
- Core workqueue package files
- Sample controller (reference implementation)
- Multiple production controllers (Job, Certificate, Namespace, EndpointSlice, etc.)

The answer.json file contains complete details with file paths, symbol definitions, and the reconcile loop chain.

The implementation (rateLimitingType) wraps a TypedDelayingInterface and uses a TypedRateLimiter to determine when items should be added back to the queue.\\n\\n4. **Rate Limiter Strategies (default_rate_limiters.go)**: Multiple rate limiting strategies are available:\\n   - TypedItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter: Implements exponential backoff (baseDelay * 2^num_failures) with a maximum delay cap. Returns 0 requeues (no per-item state).\\n   - TypedMaxOfRateLimiter: Composes multiple rate limiters and returns the worst-case (maximum) delay.\\n   - TypedItemFastSlowRateLimiter: Allows a configurable number of fast retries (fastDelay) before switching to slow retries (slowDelay).\\n   - DefaultTypedControllerRateLimiter: Combines ItemExponentialFailureRateLimiter (5ms base, 1000s max) with BucketRateLimiter (10 qps, 100 bucket) using MaxOfRateLimiter.\\n\\nThe **Controller Reconcile Loop Pattern** is consistently implemented across Kubernetes controllers:\\n1. On success, calls queue.Forget(item); on error, calls queue.AddRateLimited(item) for retry\\n5.
